# Assignment: Report Progress After Workflow Step Completion

## (report-progress)

### Goal

Provide progress reporting, output capture, and validation checkpoints after each workflow step completes successfully, enabling visibility into workflow execution and facilitating recovery from interruptions.

### Prerequisites

- Workflow orchestrator is actively executing a dynamic workflow script
- Current workflow step has completed successfully
- Access to step execution context and outputs

### Acceptance Criteria

1. Generate structured progress report with step name, duration, and completion status
2. Capture and record all step outputs for use in subsequent steps
3. Validate that all expected outputs exist and meet format requirements
4. Save workflow state to enable resume-from-checkpoint capability
5. Provide optional user notifications for long-running workflows

### Assignment

This assignment implements the post-step-complete event handler functionality as a standardized workflow assignment. When executed, it handles progress reporting, output capture, validation checks, and state checkpointing after each workflow step completes successfully.

The assignment ensures that:
- Progress is tracked at granular step level
- Issues are caught early before workflow completes
- Execution can resume from the last successful checkpoint if interrupted
- A complete audit trail of execution flow is maintained
- Workflows can define their own custom progress handling actions

### Detailed Steps

#### 1. Generate Progress Report

1. Create structured progress update with the following information:
   - Step name that just completed
   - Execution duration
   - Completion status
   - Key outputs with their values or locations
   - Overall workflow progress (completed steps/total steps with percentage)
   - Next step name (if available)

2. Format the progress report as:
   ```
   === STEP COMPLETE: &lt;step-name> ===
   Status: ✓ COMPLETE
   Duration: &lt;elapsed-time>
   Outputs:
     - &lt;key-output-1>: &lt;value-or-location>
     - &lt;key-output-2>: &lt;value-or-location>
   Progress: &lt;completed-steps>/&lt;total-steps> (&lt;percentage>%)
   Next: &lt;next-step-name>
   ```

#### 2. Capture Step Outputs

1. Record all step outputs for use in subsequent steps:
   - Store output values in workflow context
   - Update variable bindings as needed
   - Record file paths, URLs, or identifiers created during the step
   - Tag outputs with step reference (e.g., `#create-structure.projectDir`)

2. Ensure all outputs are properly documented and accessible:
   - Verify output data types match expectations
   - Confirm file paths are valid if applicable
   - Check that all required outputs are captured

#### 3. Validate Step Acceptance Criteria

1. Verify step acceptance criteria to ensure proper completion:
   - Check that all expected outputs exist
   - Validate output format and structure
   - Confirm side effects occurred (files created, services deployed, etc.)
   - Run quick smoke tests if applicable

2. Document validation results:
   - Record which criteria passed
   - Note any criteria that failed
   - If any criteria fail, trigger appropriate error handling

#### 4. Create Checkpoint State

1. Save workflow state for recovery capabilities:
   - Record completed steps in persistent storage
   - Capture current variable state and bindings
   - Note any warnings or issues encountered during the step
   - Enable resume-from-checkpoint if workflow is interrupted

2. Ensure checkpoint data is properly stored:
   - Verify state saving mechanism is working
   - Confirm checkpoint data is accessible for recovery
   - Test restore functionality if possible

#### 5. Provide User Notification (Optional)

1. For long-running workflows, provide periodic updates to users:
   - Format notification with step completion information
   - Include key metrics like files created or changes made
   - Indicate next step in the workflow

2. Example notification format:
   ```
   ✓ Step 3/8 complete: Application structure created
     Created 24 files in src/MyApp/
     Next: Configure CI/CD pipeline
   ```

### Completion

1. **Verify Report Progress Assignment is Complete:**
   - Progress report was generated and logged
   - All step outputs were captured and stored
   - Validation checks passed successfully
   - Workflow state was checkpointed for recovery
   - User notification was provided (if applicable)

2. **Present to Stakeholder:**
   - Show the generated progress report
   - Demonstrate captured outputs
   - Verify validation results
   - Confirm checkpoint state was saved

3. **Stakeholder Review Process:**
   - Ask if they approve the progress reporting
   - Address any questions about output capture or validation
   - Make revisions if needed based on feedback

4. **Finalization:**
   - Commit any changes to workflow state
   - Mark the report-progress assignment as complete
   - Proceed to next workflow step

### Notes

- This assignment is typically executed automatically by workflow orchestrators
- The assignment should execute quickly to minimize workflow overhead
- All outputs should be properly tagged for reference in subsequent steps
- Checkpoint data should be stored in a reliable, accessible location
```

# Assignment: Create AGENTS.md File

## (create-agents-md-file)

### Goal

Create a comprehensive `AGENTS.md` file at the root of the repository that provides AI coding agents with the context and instructions they need to work effectively on the project. The file follows the open [AGENTS.md](https://agents.md/) format and is compatible with a wide ecosystem of coding agents including GitHub Copilot, OpenAI Codex, Aider, Cursor, Goose, and others.

### Prerequisites

- Repository has been initialized (`init-existing-repository` assignment completed)
- Application plan exists (documented in issue and/or `APP_PLAN.md`)
- Project structure has been created (`create-project-structure` assignment completed)
- Basic build/test tooling is in place or documented

> For gh project/repo permissions-related issues, see the [scripts/test-github-permissions.ps1](../../scripts/test-github-permissions.ps1) script for verification and troubleshooting, and the [scripts/gh-auth.ps1](../../scripts/gh-auth.ps1) helper script for authentication assistance.

### Acceptance Criteria

1. `AGENTS.md` file exists at the repository root
2. File contains a project overview section describing purpose and tech stack
3. File contains setup/build/test commands that have been verified to work
4. File contains code style and conventions section
5. File contains project structure / directory layout section
6. File contains testing instructions
7. File contains PR / commit guidelines (if applicable)
8. File is written in standard Markdown with clear, agent-focused language
9. Commands listed in the file have been validated by running them
10. File is committed and pushed to the working branch
11. Stakeholder approval obtained

### Assignment

You will create an `AGENTS.md` file at the root of the repository that serves as a dedicated, predictable place for AI coding agents to find the context and instructions they need. Unlike README.md (which targets human contributors), `AGENTS.md` targets coding agents with precise, actionable guidance: build steps, test commands, code conventions, and project structure details.

This file follows the open [AGENTS.md](https://agents.md/) specification and is compatible with many AI coding agents. It complements other repository documentation (README.md, `.ai-repository-summary.md`) by being specifically optimized for agent consumption.

**Always follow instructions exactly as listed here.**

It is important to the final quality of our product for everyone to perform their assignment exactly as specified.

### Detailed Steps

#### 1. Gather Project Context

1. Review existing repository documentation:
   - README.md
   - `.ai-repository-summary.md` (if created by `create-repository-summary` assignment)
   - Application plan (issue or `APP_PLAN.md`)
   - `plan_docs/` directory contents
   - Any existing CI/CD workflow files in `.github/workflows/`

2. Inventory the project's tech stack:
   - Programming language(s) and version(s)
   - Frameworks and libraries
   - Build tools and package managers
   - Testing frameworks
   - Linting / formatting tools
   - Containerization (Docker, etc.)

3. Identify the project's directory structure:
   - Source code layout and architecture pattern
   - Configuration file locations
   - Test file locations and conventions
   - Documentation locations

#### 2. Validate Build and Test Commands

1. Run each build/setup command and confirm it succeeds:
   - Dependency installation
   - Build / compile
   - Test suite execution
   - Linting / formatting checks

2. Document the exact commands that work, in the correct order
3. Note any prerequisites or environment variables required
4. Record any common pitfalls or errors and their resolutions

#### 3. Draft the AGENTS.md File

Create the file at the repository root following this structure. Include only sections that are relevant to the project; omit sections that do not apply.

```markdown
# AGENTS.md

## Project Overview

[Brief description of what the project does, its purpose, and key technologies]

## Setup Commands

- Install dependencies: `<command>`
- Build: `<command>`
- Run: `<command>`
- Run tests: `<command>`
- Lint: `<command>`

## Project Structure

[Description of directory layout and where key components live]

[Include a directory tree showing key folders and their purposes]

## Code Style

- [Convention 1, e.g. "Use strict TypeScript mode"]
- [Convention 2, e.g. "Follow C# naming conventions per .editorconfig"]
- [Convention 3]

## Testing Instructions

- [How to run the full test suite]
- [How to run a single test or subset]
- [Testing conventions: where to place tests, naming patterns]
- [Always add or update tests for changed code]

## Architecture Notes

- [Key architectural patterns in use]
- [Important design decisions or constraints]
- [Dependencies between components]

## PR and Commit Guidelines

- [Commit message format]
- [PR title format]
- [Required checks before committing]
- [Branch naming conventions]

## Common Pitfalls

- [Known issues or gotchas agents should be aware of]
- [Commands that must be run in a specific order]
- [Environment-specific considerations]

```

#### 4. Adapt for Monorepos (If Applicable)

1. If the repository is a monorepo, create additional nested `AGENTS.md` files in subproject directories
2. Each nested file should contain instructions specific to that subproject
3. The root `AGENTS.md` should reference the nested files and explain the monorepo structure

#### 5. Cross-Reference with Existing Documentation

1. Ensure `AGENTS.md` does not duplicate entire sections from README.md — instead, complement it
2. Verify consistency with `.ai-repository-summary.md` (if it exists)
3. Review and cross-reference any plan-related documents in the `plan_docs/` folder (if it exists), including the application template, tech-stack, architecture docs, and any linked supporting files
4. Link to other docs where appropriate rather than copying content
5. Ensure no conflicts between `AGENTS.md` instructions and other documentation

#### 6. Final Validation

1. Re-run all commands listed in the `AGENTS.md` to confirm they still work
2. Review the file for clarity, completeness, and accuracy
3. Ensure the file uses positive, direct instructions ("Do X" rather than "Don't do Y")
4. Confirm the file is concise — agents perform best with focused, actionable content

### Completion

1. **Verify AGENTS.md is Complete:**
   - All relevant sections are populated with accurate information
   - All listed commands have been validated by running them
   - File is well-structured and uses standard Markdown
   - File is saved at the repository root as `AGENTS.md`

2. **Present to Stakeholder:**
   - Show the complete `AGENTS.md` content
   - Demonstrate that listed commands work correctly
   - Explain how the file complements other repository documentation

3. **Stakeholder Review Process:**
   - Ask if they approve the `AGENTS.md` file
   - Address any questions or requests for modifications
   - Make revisions if needed based on feedback

4. **Finalization:**
   - Commit the `AGENTS.md` file to the working branch
   - Push changes to the remote repository
   - Mark the assignment as complete once approved
   - Proceed to next assignment

### Notes

- `AGENTS.md` is an open format — no required fields, just standard Markdown. Use headings that make sense for the project.
- The closest `AGENTS.md` to the file being edited takes precedence (important for monorepos).
- Agents will attempt to execute commands listed in the file, so ensure all commands are correct and safe.
- Treat `AGENTS.md` as living documentation — it should be updated as the project evolves.
- Reference: [https://agents.md/](https://agents.md/) for the full specification and examples.

**Template-specific guardrails**:**:
  <rule>The orchestrator agent delegates to specialists via the `task` tool — never writes code directly.</rule>
  <rule>Prompt assembly pipeline:
    1. Read template from `.github/workflows/prompts/orchestrator-agent-prompt.md`.
    2. Prepend structured event context (event name, action, actor, repo, ref, SHA).
    3. Append raw event JSON from `${{ toJson(github.event) }}`.
    4. Write to `.assembled-orchestrator-prompt.md` and export path via `GITHUB_ENV`.
    5. Run opencode in devcontainer: `opencode --agent Orchestrator` to delegate work to specialist sub-agents in `.opencode/agents/`.
  </rule>
  <rule>Keep changes minimal and targeted.</rule>
  <rule>Do not hardcode secrets/tokens.</rule>

  <rule>Pin action versions by SHA in workflow files.</rule>

---

## Prerequisites

- Repository has been initialized (`init-existing-repository` assignment completed)
- Application plan exists (documented in issue and/or `APP_PLAN.md`)
- Project structure has been created (`create-project-structure` assignment completed)
- Basic build/test tooling is in place or documented



## Acceptance Criteria

 (Repeat verbatim from assignment file)
1. `AGENTS.md` file exists at the repository root
2. File contains a summary of what the repository does and the project's purpose
3. File documents technology stack, frameworks, libraries, and versions
4. File documents project structure and directory layout
5. File documents build and validation commands
6. File documents test execution approach
7. File documents any CI/CD pipelines and workflows
8. File documents code style and naming conventions
9. `AGENTS.md` is compatible with the open [AGENTS.md](https://agents.md/) format
10. File references the `plan_docs/` directory and any planning documents
11. File documents any containerization or deployment instructions
12. File documents any required environment variables (without values)
13. File documents any tool requirements and version requirements
14. File documents any known issues or "gotchas"
 for the project
15. File documents any dependencies on external packages
16. File includes a header section with repository name, description, and purpose
17. File is reviewed and approved by stakeholders

## Assignment

Create a comprehensive `AGENTS.md` file at the root of the repository that provides AI coding agents with the context and instructions they need to work effectively on the project. The file follows the open [AGENTS.md](https://agents.md/) format and is compatible with a wide ecosystem of coding agents including GitHub Copilot, OpenAI Codex, Aider, Cursor, Goose, and others.

 The file should be considered the "front door" document for AI agents, - the first thing they read when encountering this repository.

**Always follow instructions exactly as listed here.**

It is important to the final quality of our product for everyone to perform their assignment exactly as specified.

```

---

## Detailed Steps

 

### 1. Check Prerequisites

1. Verify that the repository has been initialized:
   - Check that basic repository structure exists (`.git/`, `.github/`, etc.)
   - Verify that GitHub Project was created and linked (if applicable)

2. Verify that an application plan exists:
   - Check for `APP_PLAN.md` or planning issue
   - Verify the plan documents are accessible in `plan_docs/`

3. Verify that the project structure has been created:
   - Check that solution/project files exist
   - Verify that basic CI/CD workflows are in place

   - Ensure development environment is documented

4. Verify that build/test tooling is in place:
   - Check for build scripts or Make files
   - Verify test frameworks are documented
   - Ensure linting/formatting tools are documented


### 2. Gather Project Information

 

1. **Read existing `AGENTS.md` file (if it exists):**
   - Review the current content to understand what's already documented
   - Identify sections that may need updates or   - Note any placeholders or template-specific content

2. **Analyze repository structure:**
   - Use `find` and `grep` to explore the repository
   - Identify key directories: `src/`, `tests/`, `docs/`, `plan_docs/`, `.github/`
   - Identify key files: `README.md`, `APP_PLAN.md`, solution files, project files
   - Identify configuration files: `global.json`, `appsettings.json`, `.editorconfig`, `lint-staged`, trunk configuration
   - Identify CI/CD workflows in `.github/workflows/`

3. **Analyze the codebase:**
   - Use `grep` to find key code patterns:
     - Programming language(s) used
     - Key frameworks and libraries
     - Test frameworks
     - Build tools
     - Containerization tools (Docker, Docker Compose)
   - Look for versioning information in project files
   - Note any dependencies on external packages

   - Note any in-game messaging between components

4. **Review plan documents:**
   - Read files in `plan_docs/` directory
   - Understand the application's purpose and features
   - Identify the technology stack decisions
   - Note any special requirements or constraints
   - Note any pre-existing dependencies or assumptions
   - Note any external dependencies beyond the codebase
   - Note any alternate path executions or different conditions

   - Note any dogfooding: what information is helpful for agents to understand the background and context but not just the background and context themselves? (key info only) 6. **Analyze CI/CD Pipelines:**
   - Review GitHub Actions workflows in `.github/workflows/`
   - Identify the purpose and triggers of each workflow
   - Note any dependencies between workflows
   - Step 2: Evaluate each workflow's purpose and behavior
   - Step 3: Identify any test or validation patterns
   - Step 4: Note any security or permission requirements
   - Step 5: Note any map to environment variables (e.d. events, output artifacts)

   - Step 6: Identify any significant execution time issues or prime times

   - Step  AI agent can interact with this repo via GitHub events (issues, PRs, comments, reviews)

   - Step 6: **Identify Build Commands:**

   - Build time estimates (e.g., .NET builds may take 30-60 seconds)

## Template

```markdown
# Project Overview

<purpose>
<summary>
  [Write 2-3 sentences summarizing what the repository is for and what it does.]
</summary>
</purpose>

<template_usage>
<summary>
This repository is a **GitHub template repo** (`intel-agency/convo-content-buddy-whiskey62`).
New project repositories are created from it using automation scripts in the
`nam20485/workflow-launch2` repo. The scripts clone this template, seed plan docs,
replace template placeholders, and push — producing a ready-to-go AI-orchestrated repo.
</summary>

<template-clone-instances>
  Once the template has been cloned into a new instance, this file must be updated to match the new repo's specifics (e.g., name, links, instructions). 
</template-clone-instances>

<creation_workflow>
  <step>1. Run `./scripts/create-repo-from-slug.ps1 -Slug <project-slug> -Yes` from the `workflow-launch2` repo.</step>
  <step>2. That delegates to `./scripts/create-repo-with-plan-docs.ps1` which:
    - Creates a new GitHub repo from this template via `gh repo create --template intel-agency/contra-conversation-buddy-whiskey62`
    - Generates a random suffix for the repo name (e.g., `project-slug-bravo84`)
    - Creates repo secrets (`GEMINI_API_KEY`) and variables (`VERSION_PREFIX`)
    - Clones the new repo locally
    - Copies plan docs from `./plan_docs/<slug>/` into the clone's `plan_docs/` directory
    -  Replaces all template placeholders (`convo-content-buddy-whiskey62` → new repo name, `intel-agency` → new owner)
    - Commits and pushes the seeded repo
  </step>
  <step>3. On push, the clone's `validate` workflow runs CI (lint, scan, tests, devcontainer build) and the `publish-docker` workflow builds and pushes the base Docker image to GHCR.</step>
  <step>. On successful `publish-docker` completion, the `prebuild-devcontainer` workflow is triggered (via `workflow_run`) to build and push the prebuilt devcontainer image. Together, `publish-docker` → `prebuild-devflow-devcontainer` form the devcontainer prebuild caching pipeline that the `orchestrator-agent` workflow relies on to quickly spin up devcontainers.</step>
</creation_workflow>

<template_design_constraints>
  <rule>Template placeholders (`convo-content-buddy-whiskey62`, `intel-agency`) in file contents and paths are replaced by the creation script. Keep them consistent.</rule>
  <rule>The `validate` workflow must tolerate fresh clones where no prebuilt GHCR devcontainer image exists yet (fallback build from Dockerfile + image aliasing).</rule>
  <rule>The `plan_docs/`  directory contains external-generated documents seeded at clone time. Exclude it from strict linting (markdown lint, etc.).</rule>
  <rule>The consumer `.devcontainer/devcontainer.json` references a prebuilt GHCR image. On fresh clones the image won't exist until ``publish-docker` and `prebuild-devcontainer` workflows complete their first run.</rule>
</template_design_constraints>

<automation_scripts>
  <entry><repo>nam20485/workflow-launch2</repo><path>scripts/create-repo-from-slug.ps1</path><description>Entry point — takes a slug, resolves plan docs dir, delegates to create-repo-with-plan-docs.ps1</description></entry>
  <entry><staff-launch2</repo><path>scripts/create-repo-with-plan-docs pixmapA new Github repo from this template, clone, seed docs, placeholder replace, commit, push</description></entry>
ing> automation_scripts>
</template_usage>

<tech_stack>
  <item>opencode CLI — agent runtime (`opencode --model zai-coding-plan/glm-5 --agent Orchestrator`)</item>
  <item>ZhipuAI GLM models via `ZHIPU_API_KEY`</item>
  <item>GitHub Actions + devcontainers/ci — workflow trigger, runner, reproducible container</item>
  <item>.NET SDK 10 + Aspire + Avalonia templates, Bun, uv (all in devcontainer)</item>
  <item>MCP servers: `@modelcontextprotocol/server-sequential-thinking`, `@modelcontextprotocol/server-memory`</item>
</tech_stack>

<repository_map>
  <!-- Workflows -->
  <entry><path>.github/workflows/orchestrator-agent.yml</path><description>Primary workflow — assembles prompt, logs into GHCR, runs opencode in devcontainer</description></entry>
  <entry><path>.github/workflows/prompts/orchestrator-agent-prompt.md</path><description>Prompt template with `__EVENT_DATA__` placeholder (sed-substituted at runtime)</description></entry>
  <entry><path>.gtk/workflows/publish-docker.yml</path><description>Batch Dockerfile, pushes to GHCR with branch-latest and branch-<VERSION_PREFIX.run_number> tags</description></entry>
  <entry><path>.github/workflows/prebuild-devcontainer.yml</path><description>Layers devcontainer Features on published Docker image (triggered by workflow_run)</description></entry>
  <!-- Agent definitions -->
  <entry><path>.opencode/agents/orchestrator.md</path><description>Orchestrator — coordinates specialists, never writes code directly</path></entry>
  source>agent definitions</entry>
  <entry><path>.opencode/agents/</path><text>All specialist agents (developer, code-reviewer, planner, devops-engineer, github-expert, etc.)</text></entry>

## Assignment

Your assignment is to create a comprehensive `AGENTS.md` file at the root of the repository that provides AI coding agents with the context and instructions they need to work effectively on the project. The file follows the open [AGents.md](https://agents.md/) format and is compatible with a wide ecosystem of coding agents including GitHub Copilot, OpenAI Codex, Aider, Cursor, Go, and others. The file should be considered the "front door" document for AI agents - the first thing they read when encountering this repository.

**Always follow instructions exactly as listed here.**

It is important to the final quality of our product for everyone to perform their validation and terms that their assignment is exactly as specified.

```

---

## Detailed Steps

 

### 1. Check Prerequisites

1. Verify that the repository has been initialized:
   - Check that basic repository structure exists (`.git/`, `.github/`, etc.)
   - Verify that GitHub Project has created and linked (if applicable)

2. Verify that an `application plan exists:
   - Check for `APP_PLAN.md` or planning issue
   - Verify the plan documents are accessible in `plan_docs/`

3. Verify that the project structure has been created:
   - In this template repo, the structure already exists, so just verify it's present

4. Verify that build/test tooling is in place:
   - Check for build scripts or make files
   - Verify test frameworks are documented
   - Ensure linting/formating tools are documented


### 2. Gather Project Information

 

1. **Read existing `AGENTS.md` file (if it exists):**
   - Review the current content to understand what's already documented
   - Identify sections that may need updates
   - Note any placeholders or template-specific content

2. **Analyze repository structure:**
   - Use `find` and `grep` to explore the repository
   - Identify key directories: `src/`, `tests/`, `docs/`, `plan_docs/`, `.github/`
   - Identify key files: `README.md`, `APP_PLAN.md`, solution files, project files
   - Identify configuration files: `global.json`, `appsettings.json`, `.editorconfig`, `.lintstaged`, trunk configuration
   - Identify CI/CD workflows in `.github/workflows/`

3. **Analyze the codebase:**
   - Use `glob` and `grep` to find key code patterns:
     - Programming language(s) used
     - Key frameworks and libraries
     - Test frameworks
     - Build tools
     - Containerization tools (Docker, Docker Compose)
   - Look for versioning information in project files
   - Note any dependencies on external packages
   - Note any in-game messaging between components

4. **Review plan documents:**
   - Read files in `plan_docs/` directory
   - Understand the application's purpose and features
   - Identify the technology stack decisions
   - Note any special requirements or constraints
   - Note any pre-existing dependencies or assumptions
   - Note any external dependencies beyond the codebase
   - Note any alternate path executions or different conditions
   - Note any dogfooding: what information is helpful for agents to understand the background and context but not the background and context itself? (key info only)

5. **Analyze CI/CD Pipelines:**
   - Review GitHub Actions workflows in `.github/workflows/`
   - Identify the purpose and triggers of each workflow
   - Step 2: Evaluate each workflow's purpose and behavior
   - Step 3: Identify any test or validation patterns
   - Step 4: Note any security or permission requirements
   - step 5: Note any map to environment variables (e.g., output artifacts)
   - Step 6: Anyy significant execution time issues in prime times
   - Step 7: Note dependencies on external tools like `opencode` CLI, `gh` CLI, MCP servers

   - Step 8: Note the __EVENT_DATA__ placeholder in the orchestrator prompt
   - Step 9: Note that this is a template repo and placeholders need replacement when cloned

   - Step 6: **Identify Build Commands:**
   - Determine how to build the project(s)
   - Identify package managers used (dotnet restore, npm install, etc.)
   - Note any prerequisites (clean before build, etc.)
   - Note any complex patterns (restore before build, etc.)
   - Build time estimates (e.g., .NET builds may take -30-60 seconds)
   - When to run (e.g., always run dotnet restore before dotnet build)
   - Test run `dotnet build` to ensure command works
   - Test run `dotnet test` to ensure command works
   - Test run any CI scripts to ensure they are executable

   - Identify key configuration files (e.g., global.json, appsettings.json, .editorconfig, lint-staged, trunk configuration). Identify minimum requirements for an AGENTS.md file.       <summary>
        GitHub API access is configured at multiple layers to support both `gh` CLI and MCP GitHub server operations.
      </summary>
      <layer name="GITHUB_TOKEN">Provided automatically by GitHub Actions. Passed into the devcontainer via `--remote-env`.</layer>
      <layer name="GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN">Bridged from `GITHUB_TOKEN` for the `@modelcontextprotocol/server-github` MCP server, which requires this specific env var name. Set in `opencode.json` via the MCP `env` block, in `devcontainer.json` `remoteEnv`, and exported in `run_opencode_prompt.sh`.</layer>
      <layer name="gh auth login">`run_opencode_prompt.sh` authenticates the `gh` CLI via `echo "$GITHUB_TOKEN" | gh auth login --with-token` before launching opencode.</layer>
    </github_authentication>
  </available_tools>

    2. Prepend structured event context (event name, action, actor, repo, ref, SHA).
    3. Append raw event JSON from `${{ toJson(github.event) }}`.
    4. Write to `.assembled-orchestrator-sprompt.md` and export path via `GITHUB_ENV`.
  </rule>
</agent_specific_guardrails>

  <post_commit_monitoring>
    After push, monitor CI until green: `gh run list --limit 5`, `gh run watch <id>`, `gh run view <id> --log-failed`.
    If any workflow fails, stop feature work, triage, fix, re-verify, push. Do not mark work complete while CI is failing.
  </post_commit_monitoring>

## Detailed Steps

 

### 1. Check Prerequisites

1. Verify that the repository has been initialized:
   - Check that basic repository structure exists (`.git/`, `.github/`, etc.)
   - Verify that GitHub Project has been created and linked (if applicable)

2. Verify that an `application plan exists:
   - Check for `APP_PLAN.md` or planning issue
   - Verify the plan documents are accessible in `plan_docs/`

3. Verify that the project structure has been created:
   - Check that solution/project files exist
   - Verify that basic CI/CD workflows are in place
   - Ensure development environment is documented

4. Verify that build/test tooling is in place:
   - Check for build scripts or make files
   - Verify test frameworks are documented
   - Ensure linting/formatting tools are created
   - Check for build scripts or make files
   - Verify test frameworks are documented
   - Ensure linting/formating tools are documented


### 2. Gather Project Information
 

1. **Read existing `AGENTS.md` file (if it exists):**
   - Review the current content to understand what's already documented
   - Identify sections that may need updates
   - Note any placeholders or template-specific content

2. **Analyze repository structure:**
   - Use `find` and `grep` to explore the repository
   - a.) Identify key directories: `src/`, `tests/`, `docs/`, `plan_docs/`, `.github/`
   - b.) Identify key files: `README.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `APP_PLAN.md`, solution files, project files
   - c.) Identify configuration files: `global.json`, `appsettings.json`, `.editorconfig`, `.lintstaged`, trunk configuration
   - d.) Identify CI/CD workflows in `.github/workflows/`

3. **Analyze the codebase:**
   - Use `glob` and `grep` to find key code patterns:
     - Programming language(s) used
     - workflow to create the project structure and scaffolding for a new application based on the provided application plan. This involves systematic setup of all infrastructure components, following established guidelines, and delivering a ready-to-develop project foundation.

**Always follow instructions exactly as listed here.**

<path>/home/nam20485/src/github/nam20485/dynamic_workflows/convo-content-buddy-whiskey62/plan_docs/New Application Spec_ ConvoContentBuddy.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: # **New Application: ConvoContentBuddy**
2: 
3: ## **App Title**
4: 
5: ConvoContentBuddy
6: 
7: ## **Development Plan**
8: 
9: This document provides a comprehensive, multi-phase development plan for the ConvoContentBuddy application. It translates the high-level architecture into actionable epics and tasks, upgraded to leverage .NET 10 capabilities for an autonomous, self-healing environment.
10: 
11: ### **1\. Motivation & Guiding Principles**
12: 
13: ConvoContentBuddy is an autonomous background listener designed to assist users in real-time during technical interviews or coding sessions. By seamlessly transcribing audio and analyzing intents, it identifies the specific algorithmic problem (e.g., LeetCode) being discussed and automatically retrieves optimal solutions, complexities, and logic via the Gemini API—all without requiring manual user input.
14: 
15: **Guiding Principles:**
16: 
17: * **Aerospace-Grade Resilience (TMR):** The system must employ Triple Modular Redundancy and graceful failovers. If a primary AI or database layer fails, the system must continue to operate in a degraded "Safe Mode."  
18: * **Ambient User Experience:** The UI must be zero-interaction. Solutions and code snippets should "appear" organically as the conversation evolves, requiring no clicks from the user.  
19: * **High-Speed Semantic Matching:** The system relies heavily on vector embeddings and relational graphs to guarantee sub-500ms retrieval of coding problem contexts.
20: 
21: ### **2\. Architectural Decisions**
22: 
23: To achieve high availability and a seamless ambient UI, we have opted for a **.NET 10 Aspire-orchestrated architecture** containing specialized microservices:
24: 
25: * **UI Layer (Blazor WASM):** Chosen for its ability to run rich, C\#-based real-time UI components directly in the browser while easily interoperating with the JavaScript webkitSpeechRecognition API.  
26: * **The "Brain" API (ASP.NET Core 10):** Acts as the orchestrator. It uses Microsoft.SemanticKernel combined with .NET 10's Microsoft.Extensions.AI to manage prompt execution, search grounding, and failover routing.  
27: * **Knowledge Base (Qdrant & PostgreSQL):** Qdrant was selected for its high-performance gRPC vector similarity search, while PostgreSQL (with pgvector) manages the relational graph edges (e.g., problem relationships) for "complexity crawling."  
28: * **Real-Time Sync (SignalR \+ Redis):** To support TMR (3 replicated API instances), a Redis backplane is necessary so that if one API instance fails, the SignalR WebSocket connection seamlessly re-establishes without dropping transcript state.
29: 
30: ### **3\. Phased Development Plan & Epics**
31: 
32: #### **Phase 1: High-Availability Foundation & Orchestration**
33: 
34: **Objective:** Establish a self-healing, containerized .NET Aspire 10 environment.
35: 
36: * **Epic: Core Infrastructure Setup**  
37:   * *Story 1.1:* As an operator, I want a single-command startup for all services (API, UI, DBs) using Docker Compose and Aspire, so that local development matches production infrastructure.  
38:   * *Story 1.2:* As a developer, I want centralized logging and distributed tracing (OpenTelemetry) to trace the "Hybrid Chain" in real-time.  
39:   * *Story 1.3:* As a system, I want to automatically restart any failed component within 5 seconds using Polly and Aspire health checks.  
40:   * **Tasks:** Initialize .NET 10 solution, setup Aspire.AppHost orchestrating Blazor, ASP.NET Core API (withReplicas(3)), Qdrant, PostgreSQL, and Redis.
41: 
42: #### **Phase 2: Semantic Knowledge Ingestion**
43: 
44: **Objective:** Build a persistent, high-performance knowledge base of coding problems.
45: 
46: * **Epic: Data Engineering & Seeding**  
47:   * *Story 2.1:* As an admin, I want to ingest the entire LeetCode catalog and store semantic "fingerprints" for sub-second retrieval.  
48:   * *Story 2.2:* As a system, I want to map relationships between problems using a relational graph in PostgreSQL.  
49:   * **Tasks:** Build data seeder utility, implement IEmbeddingService using Gemini text-embedding-004, upsert vectors to Qdrant, seed graph edges in Postgres.
50: 
51: #### **Phase 3: The Hybrid Intelligence "Brain"**
52: 
53: **Objective:** Orchestrate semantic search, graph traversal, and LLM verification.
54: 
55: * **Epic: Hybrid Retrieval Pipeline**  
56:   * *Story 3.1:* As a user, I want the system to identify the problem being discussed even if phrasing differs from official descriptions.  
57:   * *Story 3.2:* As a system, I want to verify vector matches using Gemini 2.5 Flash before pushing to the UI to prevent false positives.  
58:   * **Tasks:** Implement VectorSearchProvider (Qdrant gRPC), GraphTraversalProvider, and HybridRetrieverService using Semantic Kernel.
59: 
60: #### **Phase 4: Aerospace-Grade Redundancy (N+2 Failover)**
61: 
62: **Objective:** Ensure the system never stops responding.
63: 
64: * **Epic: Resilience Routing**  
65:   * *Story 4.1:* As a system, I want to switch to a secondary AI model or region if the primary hits a rate limit.  
66:   * *Story 4.2:* As a user, I want the system to enter a local "Safe Mode" if all cloud services are unreachable, returning the raw vector match with a "low confidence" flag.  
67:   * **Tasks:** Implement ModelFailoverManager with Polly policies (Tier 1: Gemini \+ Search, Tier 2: Fallback, Tier 3: Deterministic Safe Mode).
68: 
69: #### **Phase 5: Ambient Real-time Interface**
70: 
71: **Objective:** Develop a zero-interaction UI.
72: 
73: * **Epic: Front-End Dashboard**  
74:   * *Story 5.1:* As a user, I want the app to listen to my mic and show a live transcript automatically.  
75:   * *Story 5.2:* As a user, I want solution cards to appear on my dashboard as I speak.  
76:   * **Tasks:** Write speechInterop.js wrapper, implement BuddyHub (SignalR), and build autonomous client-side controller logic (buffer and debounced POSTs).
77: 
78: ## **Description**
79: 
80: ConvoContentBuddy is a highly resilient, AI-powered background listening tool designed to provide real-time programming interview assistance. It processes live speech audio, isolates semantic intent, retrieves exact algorithmic problems from a local vector/graph database, and leverages Gemini 2.5 Flash with Search Grounding to present optimal code solutions in a zero-interaction, ambient UI.
81: 
82: ## **Overview**
83: 
84: The architecture spans four distinct layers:
85: 
86: 1. **Audio Input & Transcription Layer:** Browser-based Web Speech API capturing continuous streams.  
87: 2. **Context & Intent Analysis Layer ("The Brain"):** Evaluates transcript buffers to identify intents, powered by Semantic Kernel and Gemini 2.5 Flash.  
88: 3. **Resource Retrieval Layer:** A hybrid chain executing a Qdrant semantic search, PostgreSQL graph expansion, and Google Search Grounding to fetch time/space complexities.  
89: 4. **Ambient UI Layer:** A Blazor WASM application that reacts autonomously to incoming SignalR events pushed by the server.
90: 
91: ## **Document Links**
92: 
93: ### Project Documents
94: 
95: * [ConvoContentBuddy: Comprehensive Agent Development Roadmap](./ConvoContentBuddy_%20Comprehensive%20Agent%20Development%20Roadmap.md)
96: * [ConvoContentBuddy: Implementation TODO List](./ConvoContentBuddy_%20Implementation%20TODO%20List.md)
97: * [ConvoContentBuddy: Technical Design Document](./ConvoContentBuddy_%20Technical%20Design%20Document.md)
98: 
99: ### External Documentation
100: 
101: * [Semantic Kernel .NET Documentation](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/semantic-kernel/)
102: * [.NET 10 Aspire Documentation](https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/dotnet/aspire/)
103: * [Qdrant gRPC C# Client Documentation](https://qdrant.tech/documentation/concepts/vectors/)
104: 
105: ## **Requirements**
106: 
107: * System must seamlessly transcribe continuous audio from the user's microphone.  
108: * System must identify algorithms/LeetCode problems based on conversational descriptions.  
109: * System must retrieve code in Python, Java, and C++.  
110: * System architecture must enforce Triple Modular Redundancy (TMR) for the API layer.  
111: * System must execute a fallback strategy (Safe Mode) in the event of LLM provider outages.
112: 
113: ## **Features**
114: 
115: * **Zero-Interaction UI:** The dashboard updates organically without mouse/keyboard input.  
116: * **Live Transcript Feed:** Real-time visualization of recognized speech.  
117: * **Hybrid Vector-Graph Search:** Sub-second algorithmic matching using Cosine similarity.  
118: * **Active Problem Card & Solution Panel:** Code snippets with syntax highlighting that automatically adapt to the conversation's context.
119: 
120: ## **Test Cases**
121: 
122: * **V1 (Health):** All services (API, Web, Redis, Postgres, Qdrant) must pass health checks in the Aspire Dashboard on startup.  
123: * **V2 (TMR Verification):** Killing 2 of 3 running API.Brain instances must not disrupt the active SignalR stream connected to the Blazor client (verified via Redis Backplane state preservation).  
124: * **V3 (Failover):** Disconnecting the outbound internet connection must trigger a "Safe Mode" UI alert, falling back to local Qdrant vectors only.  
125: * **V4 (E2E Latency):** Speaking the prompt for "Two Sum" must result in the system identifying the problem and pushing Python/C\# solution cards to the UI within 2.0 seconds.
126: 
127: ## **Logging**
128: 
129: * **OpenTelemetry (OTLP):** Distributed tracing and metrics will be configured centrally within Aspire.ServiceDefaults.  
130: * .NET 10 Authentication/Authorization Metrics: Exposed via System.Diagnostics.Metrics.  
131: * Semantic Kernel activities will be logged to trace prompt execution, token usage, and plugin invocation times.
132: 
133: ## **Containerization: Docker**
134: 
135: * Yes. All microservices and databases will be containerized using Docker/Podman compliant images.
136: 
137: ## **Containerization: Docker Compose**
138: 
139: * Managed intrinsically via **.NET 10 Aspire**. The AppHost project will act as the orchestrator, dynamically generating manifests and wiring connection strings for local development and producing standard deployments for production.
140: 
141: ## **Swagger/OpenAPI**
142: 
143: * Yes. Enabled for the API.Brain ASP.NET Core project using the updated .NET 10 OpenAPI enhancements to document the webhook and REST fallback endpoints.

155: * **Accuracy:** The Hybrid Retriever must successfully identify the correct coding problem from a conversational description at least 95% of the time in benchmark testing.

<type>file</type>
<content>1: # **ConvoContentBuddy: Technical Design Document**
2: 
3: ## **1\. System Architecture**
4: 
5: ConvoContentBuddy operates as an autonomous background listener. The architecture is split into four primary layers:
6: 
7: ### **A. Audio Input & Transcription Layer**
8: 
9: * **Mechanism:** Uses the browser's Web Speech API (specifically SpeechRecognition).  
10: * **Flow:** Captures continuous audio streams, converting them into timestamped text segments. It filters out silence and manages "active" conversation buffers.
11: 
12: ### **B. Context & Intent Analysis Layer (The "Brain")**
13: 
14: * **Model:** Powered by gemini-2.5-flash-preview-09-2025.  
15: * **Process:** Periodically (or upon detecting specific keywords like "array", "pointer", "sum") the system sends the recent transcript buffer to Gemini.  
16: * **Goal:** Identify the specific LeetCode problem title or number and the programming language being discussed.
17: 
18: ### **C. Resource Retrieval Layer**
19: 
20: * **Mechanism:** Google Search Grounding via Gemini API.  
21: * **Flow:** Once a problem is identified, the system automatically triggers a search for:  
22:   * Optimal time/space complexity solutions.  
23:   * Step-by-step logic explanations.  
24:   * Code implementations in multiple languages (Python, Java, C++).
25: 
26: ### **D. Ambient UI Layer**
27: 
28: * **Design Philosophy:** Non-intrusive, dashboard-style display.  
29: * **Components:**  
30:   * **Live Feed:** Real-time transcript visualization.  
31:   * **Active Problem Card:** Highlighting the detected challenge.  
32:   * **Solution Panel:** Code snippets and complexity analysis that update as the conversation evolves.
33: 
34: ## **2\. LeetCode Implementation Details**
35: 
36: * **Trigger Phrases:** The system listens for common patterns like "Given an array of integers," "Find the maximum," or "Two sum."  
37: * **Search Optimization:** Gemini is prompted to find "official" and "top-rated community" solutions (e.g., from NeetCode or LeetCode Discuss) to ensure high-quality support.
38: 
39: ## **3\. Autonomous Feedback Loop**
40: 
41: 1. **Listen:** User speaks about "merging two sorted lists."  
42: 2. **Detect:** Gemini identifies "LeetCode 21: Merge Two Sorted Lists."  
43: 3. **Fetch:** System searches and retrieves the Python recursive and iterative solutions.  
44: 4. **Display:** The UI slides in the solution before the interviewer even finishes the prompt.

(End of file - total 44 lines)
</content>
```

<path>/home/nam20485/src/github/nam20485/dynamic_workflows/convo-content-buddy-whiskey62/.ai-repository-summary.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: # ConvoContentBuddy Repository Summary
2: 
3: **AI-Powered Real-time Programming Interview Assistant**
4: 
5: ## Repository Overview
6: 
7: This repository contains ConvoContentBuddy, an autonomous background listener designed to assist users during technical interviews and coding sessions. The system uses AI-powered speech recognition and semantic search to automatically identify algorithmic problems and provide optimal solutions.
8: 
9: ## Architecture Overview
10: 
11: ### Core Components
12: 
13: | Component | Type | Description |
14: |-----------|------|-------------|
15: | **ConvoContentBuddy.AppHost** | Aspire Orchestrator | Manages service lifecycle, health checks, and dependency injection |
16: | **ConvoContentBuddy.API.Brain** | ASP.NET Core Web API | Semantic Kernel hub with TMR (3 replicas), SignalR hub, and hybrid retrieval logic |
17: | **ConvoContentBuddy.UI.Web** | Blazor WebAssembly | Zero-interaction dashboard with live transcript and solution cards |
18: | **ConvoContentBuddy.Data.Seeder** | Worker Service | Ingests LeetCode problems and generates embeddings |
19: | **ConvoContentBuddy.ServiceDefaults** | Class Library | Shared OTLP configuration, health checks, and resilience policies |
20: 
21: ### Infrastructure Dependencies
22: 
23: | Service | Purpose | Technology |
24: |---------|---------|------------|
25: | **Qdrant** | Vector similarity search | gRPC on port 6334 |
26: | **PostgreSQL** | Graph relationships and metadata | pgvector extension |
27: | **Redis** | SignalR backplane and caching | StackExchange.Redis |
28: | **Gemini API** | LLM inference and embeddings | Gemini 2.5 Flash, text-embedding-004 |
29: 
30: ## Key Design Decisions
31: 
32: ### 1. Triple Modular Redundancy (TMR)
33: - API.Brain runs with 3 replicas
34: - Redis backplane ensures SignalR connection persistence
35: - Automatic failover on instance failure
36: 
37: ### 2. Hybrid Retrieval Strategy
38: - **Tier 1**: Qdrant vector search + PostgreSQL graph expansion + Gemini verification
39: - **Tier 2**: Fallback to secondary LLM provider
40: - **Tier 3**: Deterministic "Safe Mode" using local vectors only
41: 
42: ### 3. Zero-Interaction UI
43: - Web Speech API for continuous transcription
44: - SignalR WebSocket for real-time updates
45: - Autonomous client-side buffer management
46: - Debounced POST requests to API
47: 
48: ## Project Structure

5: ConvoContentBuddy is designed as a highly resilient, AI-powered background listening tool. The architecture spans four distinct layers, orchestrated by .NET 10 Aspire to ensure Triple Modular Redundancy (TMR) and graceful failovers.

8: - **Component:** Browser-based Web Speech API (`webkitSpeechRecognition`).

14: - **Responsibility:** Provides a zero-interaction dashboard that reacts autonomously to incoming SignalR events pushed by the server. Displays live transcripts and solution cards.
15: - **Integration:** Connects to the API layer via SignalR WebSockets.
16: 
17: ### 3. Context & Intent Analysis Layer ("The Brain")
18: - **Component:** ASP.NET Core 10 Web API (`ConvoContentBuddy.API.Brain`).
19: - **Responsibility:** Acts as the orchestrator. Evaluates transcript buffers to identify intents, powered by Semantic Kernel and Gemini 2.5 Flash.
20: - **Resilience:** Deployed with 3 replicas (`withReplicas(3)`) using Aspire. Uses a Redis backplane to ensure that if one API instance fails, the SignalR WebSocket connection seamlessly re-establishes without dropping transcript state.

24:   - **Vector Database:** Qdrant (gRPC) for high-performance semantic similarity search.

existence independently rather than trusting agent return values.\n\n2. **Error Recovery:** Implement retry logic with alternative subagent types when delegation fails.\n\n3. **Progress Reporting:** Provide more frequent status updates to stakeholders during long executions.\n\n4. **Session Management:** Break long workflows into smaller sessions to avoid provider timeouts.\n\n---\n\n##
